SOCIALIST REPUBLIC OF QVET NM
PRIMARY EDUCATION PROJECT
PROCUREMENT
1.        The procurement of goods and works will be carried out in accordance
with Guidelines for Procurement under IBRD Loans and IDA Credits, May 1992.
Consultant services (including studies) would be selected and employed by the
Project Coordination Unit in accordance with the "Guidelines for the Uae of
Consultants by World Bank Borrowers." Standard Bank procurement documents were
reviewed with the MOET during project preparation.  In the procurement of goods
through ICB, goods manufactured in the Socialist Republic of Viet Nam may be
granted a margin of preference of 15% (or the applicable import duties, whichever
is less) for purposes of bid comparison.
Competitive Bidding Advertized Locally
2.        Local procurement procedures have not been adequately standardized or
codified, and IDA proposes to assist the Government in doing so.  For the
purposes of this project, local competitive bidding (LCB) procedures were
discussed at negotiations and are set out below.
3.        Advertising.   The Invitation for Bids shall be advertised in a
newspaper of local circulation where the civil works are to be provided, and the
goods to be supplied. In those areas where this is not possible, the Invitation
for Bids shall be posted at the respective Office of the Peoples' Committee or
such other place or places as shall be appropriate.
4.        The Invitation for Bids shall be in Vietnamese language and in such
other language which may be deemed appropriate by the Borrower's department or
agency concerned, and shall include the information referred to in the model
Invitation for Bids set forth in the Sample Bidding Documents, Procurement of
Works (in the case of civil works contracts) and Procurement of Goods (in the
case of goods), published by the Bank on December 1991 and May 1993,
respectively.
5.        With due regard of the nature of the civil works to be provided and
goods to be supplied, the time period for bid submission from invitation shall
be sufficient to allow potential bidders a reasonable time to prepare and submit
their bids. it shall be no less than 30 calendar days, unless otherwise agreed
with the Association.
6.        Eligibility.  The eligibility of bidders and the origin of goods
supplied shall be as defined under the Guidelines for Procurement under IBRD
Loans and IDA Credits (May 1992) (the Guidelines).
7.        Foreign bidders will be allowed to bid, if they wish to do so.



-216-                          Anex 20
Page 2 of 3
Nevertheless, foreign bidders may be required to have a local agent/intermediary
in Viet Nam.
9.        Bidding.   In addition to the Invitation for Bids, the Bidding
Documents shall include the following:
(a) Instructions to Bidders, including the criteria to be used for bid
evaluations;
(b) Conditions of Contract;
(c) Technical Specifications;
(d) Bid Form and Price Schedules; and
(e)  Performance Security (optional £or bids below a Dollar equivalent sum
to be agreed with the Association).
In case of civil works, the Bidding Documents shall also include BUI
of Quantities, or breakdown of lump sum price, as the case may be.
10.       Bids may be expressed in Dong or in such other foreign currency as set
forth in the Invitation for Bids. If the currency of payment set forth in the
Invitation for Bids is Dong, the Invitations may indicate that there is no
obligation on the part of the Borrower's department or agency requesting the bids
to convert into foreign currency the amounts to be paid.
11.       Bidding documents shall be in Vietnamese language or in such other
language that may be deemed appropriate by the Borrower's department or agency
concerned.
12.       Bids may be delivered by mail or by hand at the place set forth for
such purposes in the Invitation for Bids.
13.       Bids shall be opened publicly allowing representatives of the bidders
to attend if they so desire. Bids shall not be modified after bid opening except
to correct arithmetical errors; all bids shall be opened at the same time.
14.       Bids may not be rejected for the sole purpose of obtaining lower bids.
The Borrower shall consult with the Association prior to rejecting all bids or
soliciting new bids. All bids shall not be rejected and new bids invited on the
same specifications solely for the purposes of obtaining lower prices, except in
cases where the lowest evaluated bid exceeds the cost estimates by a substantial
amount. In such cases the Borrower may, as an alternative to rebidding and with
the prior concurrence of the Association, negotiate with the lowest evaluated
bidder to try to obtain a satisfactory contract, and failing a satisfactory
response, with the next lowest evaluated bidder. Rejection of all bids may be
permissible when bids are not substantially responsive or there is lack of
effective competition.
15.       In the comparison of bids between local and foreign bidders, no
domestic or regional preferences to local bidders shall apply and bids shall be
compared on delivered price inclusive of any prevailing duties.
16.       Award of the contract shall be to the lowest evaluated responsive
bidder. Price negotiation with bidders shall not be undertaken before award
except as provided in paragraph 12 above.



-217-                           Arex 20
Page 3 of 3
17.       The award of contract shall be made within the perlod specified in the
bidding documents. This period shall be determined in each case (goods or works)
depending on the complexity of the contract and the approval.
18.       A bid evaluation report shall be prepared by the Borrower's department
or agency requesting the bids setting out a record of all bids submitted, the
reasons for disqualification of any bids, the criteria, weighing and evaluation
of all responsive bids, the recommended award, and, if recommended award is to
other than the lowest price bidder, the reasons therefor. The concerned
Borrower's department or agency shall furnish the to Association an English
translation of such bid evaluation report pursuant to paragraphs 2 and 3 of
Appendix 1 to the Guidelines.
19.       Documents.  Notwithstanding the contract amount threshold set forth
in paragraph 1 (a), Part D of Schedule 3 to the Development Credit Agreement,
bidding documents for the first procurement of civil works or goods under the
procurement procedures outlined in this letter shall be subject to the
Association's prior review in accordance with paragraphs 2 and 4 of Appendix 1
to the Guidelines.

SOCIALIST REPUBLIC OF VIET NAN
PRIMARY EDUCATION PROJECT
ANNUAL. MID-TERM. AND FINAL REVIEWS
1.    In addition to normal project supervision, three kinds of special
reviews would take place under the project:
- an Annual Review, to review the progress of project implementation
over the preceding twelve months and to review the project
implementation plan for the next twelve months;
- a Mid-Term Review, to take stock of multi-year project accomplish-
ments and guide course correction of fine-tuning for the remaining
project years; and
- a Final Review, to assess overall achievement of the project's
physical and pedagogical objectives.
Each is summarized below.
Annual Reviews
2.    A review of project implementation during the preceding year and a
review of the project implementation plan for the upcoming year would take
place between October and December of each year until the project eloses. The
first review would be a Project Launch Workshop and would take place soon
after anticipated Board Approval. Annual reviews would focus principally on
year-to-year progress toward the achievement of the project's physical and
pedagogical objectives and the functioning of the various units responsible
for project implementation, but would also provide the Borrower and IDA to
discuss longer term issues on a periodic basis. The following specific tasks
would be reviewed in each Annual Review:
- Progress in mobilizing counterpart funds.
- Progress in organizing New School Committees.
- Progress in preparing school maD.
- Progress in preparing school construction plana.
- Progress in completing civil woxks.
- Previous year's experience in textbook development, production, and
distribution, including a review of the EPH's Business Plan for the
upcoming year (interalia, parameters of (i) production costs, (ii)
distribution costs, (iii) numbers produced, and (iv) numbers
purchased/rented for a fee/lent free of charge.



-235-                           ANNEX 25
Page 2 of 4
- Progress in implementation of pedagogical aspects of Ethnic
Minorities Education, specifically, the progress in producing
learning materials and training teachers for multi-graded teaching
situations, for mother-tongue literacy, and for the teaching of
Vietnamese as the national language.
- Experience with technical assistance during previous year and plans
for hiring technical assistance required in upcoming year.
- Experience with stgoY_to£r during previous year and plans for study
tours during the upcoming year.
- Progress in undertaking the Iational Sample-Based Assessment.
3.    The Annual Review of the functioning of the units responsible for
project implementation would examine:
- the staffing and functioning of the Project Coordination Unit;
- procurement performance;
. budgeting procedures;
- the timeliness and efficiency of the flow of funds;
- accounting and auditing procedures and timeliness; and
- staffing at the provincial, district, and commune levels, and spot
checks of their performance.
Mid-Term Revi
4.    The Mid-Term Review would assess the same factors as the Annual Reviews,
as well as other indicators for which changes are more likely to be observable
on a multi-year than on an annual basis. These additional factors include:
- initial results (in terms of reduced repetitition and drop-out and
improved pupil performance) among ethnic-minority pupils as a result
of the project's Ethnic Minorities Education Inputs;
- performance in carrying out the first National Sample-based
Assessment, and results;
- general results of the implementation of the project's civil works
component (by the Mid-Term Review, civil works in the 5 cities and in
the Mekong Delta should have been completed, as should the first
portion of construction in the 8 ethnic-minority provinces);
- general performance with procurement and competitive bidding;
- the quality of project-supported research being done at the Primary
Teacher Schools; and



-236-                         ANNEX 25
Page 3 of 4
- the experience with provincial and district competitions for teaching
aids produced by the teachers themselves.
The Kid-Term Review would take place during the fourth year of the project
(presumably, October 1996) and would replace the Annual Review in that year.
As needed, it would propose mid-course corrections for consideration by IDA
and the Government.
Final Review
5.    The Final Review would assess the same factors as the Annual Reviews and
the Mid-Term Review, as well as other indicators for which changes are more
likely to be observable once the project has been completed. These additional
factors include:
- performance of Parents' Associations and local People's Committees in
maintaining the civil works repaired or provided new under the
project;
- changes in pupil achievement in primary education, as shown by the
results of three National Assessments, which may be due to the impact
of the project;
- achievements and problems with ethnic-minority education, and plans
for expanding the successful aspects of the program to other ethnic
minorities; and
- the extent to which the Education Publishing House has become self-
financing, and long-term trends in proportions of pupils who buy
textbooks, rent them for a fee, or borrow them free of charge.
The Final Review would take place during the final year of the project. It
would replace the Annual Review in that year and serve as an input to the
Project Completion Report.
Methodology
6.    The Project Coordination Unit would be responsible for preparing, prior
to each Annual Review, a report on the previous year's experience and a work
plan for the upcoming year. This report would be augmented to cover the
topics listed above for the Mid-Term Review and the Final Review.
7.    Information on pupil performance would be assessed every two years
through the Project's Assessment Component. The information from the first
National Assessment would be available for the Mid-Term Review; the
information from three National Assessments would be available for the Final
Review.
8.    Data on other aspects of project implementation would be gathered,
amalgamated, and analyzed throughout project implementation under the
Project's Monitoring and Evaluation Component. This information would be
summarized annually and be made available for the Annual, Mid-Term, and Final
Reviews.



-237-                          ANNB 25
Page 4 of 4
9.    Supplementing the assessment findings and the monitoring data would be
annual education statistics collected by the Department of Finance and
Statistics of the Ministry of Education and Training, information on education
finance from the Ministry of Finance, information on project expenditures and
the flow of funds from the financial records of the Project Coordination Unit,
and interviews with technical assistants, provincial and district education
authorities, parents, teachers, pupils, and ethnic-minority leaders to assess
local commitment to and participation in the project and important aspects of
project implementation which assessment and monitoring data cannot adequately
capture.
